Little Men (33)

By Louisa May Alcott, Translated by Zheng Xiaocang (Zonghai)

"I want to save it up until I have enough to buy a violin for myself, so I can earn my own living, can't I?" he always said as he gave the money to Mr. Bhaer to keep for him.

"That is my hope, Nat; but you must get strong and well first, and put some knowledge into your musical head. Then Mr. Laurence will help you get a place, and we will all come to hear you play beautifully some day."

With congenial work to do, and sympathetic encouragement, hope grew strong, and Nat found himself happier day by day, and advanced rapidly in his music lessons. Mr. Bhaer pardoned his slowness in other things because he saw where his heart was, and knew that the boy's head was quickest there. A word about neglecting more important duties was quite sufficient, for the sight of the cherished violin lying idle for a day was a sharp reproof. The fear of quite losing his kind, wise friend spurred him on to struggle with his books; and once having proved that he could learn, he asked no more if he 'couldn't.'"

Meg loved music very much, and regarded those who could sing or play with great respect, so she often sat on the stairs outside Nat's door to listen to him practice. He knew it, and played his best for the sake of this quiet little auditor; she never disturbed him, but sewed on her bits of gay-colored stuff, or held one of her many babies, with a placid, motherly look on her face that made Aunt March wipe her eyes and softly say, "How like my dear Josie!" as she glided by, fearing to disturb the child's innocent pleasure.

Japan Implements Youth School System

Merges Remedial Schools and Youth Training Centers

(Hualian News Agency, Tokyo, 1st) The Japanese Ministry of Education will implement a new youth school system from today, merging the existing remedial schools and youth military training centers. The training subjects can be increased or decreased according to the specific circumstances of each region, divided into five major subjects, the contents of which are as follows:

(1) Moral Cultivation and Civics: Teach the essence of the national polity, the spirit of self-government, the legal system, and common sense of economics and society.

(2) General Subjects: Teach the national language, national history, geography, mathematics, and music.

(3) Vocational Subjects: Specially liaise with local industrial organizations to practice various techniques such as aquaculture, industry, commerce, and agriculture, and arbitrarily select courses according to the needs of the region.

(4) Home Economics and Sewing: Gather unmarried women to teach home economics, sewing, and handicrafts, opening up knowledge needed for family life.

(5) Physical Education: Teach gymnastics, drills, competitions, and games.

(6) Drill Subject: Special emphasis on military drills.

China Health Education Society

Shanghai Branch Established Yesterday

And a Farewell to Comrades Yu and Pang Going Abroad for Study

In order to connect people from the health and education circles in the city who are interested in health education, and to promote health education and strive for the popularization of health education in China, the China Health Education Society has appointed comrades Pan Gongzhan, Yu Songjun, and Wang Qizhang to prepare for the establishment of the Shanghai Branch. Page 19

Medical and Pharmaceutical Weekly of the Shen Bao, Discussion on Typhoid Fever 5 (Middle) (Under the Taiyang Channel) Yu Yunxiu

Similar to chest binding is fullness. The "Treatise on Typhoid Fever" says: "If the pulse is floating and tight, and purgation is performed again, the tightness turns inward, then fullness occurs. Pressing on it feels soft, it is only qi fullness." Fang Zhonghang notes: "Soft means not hard, not painful, but pliable." According to Fang's explanation, it is correct. The "Guanzi, Youguan" chapter says, "Store warmth with gentle waves." The note says, "In the first month of a ruler's reign, fullness is warm, gentle, and slow." This means that 'soft' can be interpreted as pliable. Also, in the "Jiyun" dictionary, category 28, 'Dú', 輭 (ruǎn) and 軟 (ruǎn) are interchangeable with 濡 (rú), meaning that 濡 (rú) is the same as 軟 (ruǎn). Ke Yunbo changed 濡 (rú) to 硬 (yìng), and Xu Lingtai interpreted 濡 (rú) as damp, both of which are incorrect. The "Treatise on Typhoid Fever" also says, "Fullness below the heart, pressing on it feels soft," and "Only fullness without pain is called fullness." Considering all these passages, the fullness described in the "Treatise on Typhoid Fever" is a mild form of the tympanites symptom of typhoid fever. If the tympanites is severe, pressing on it does not feel much different, and the danger is greater. Perhaps what is called visceral binding refers to this?

After chest binding, what should be noted is heat entering the blood chamber. In the "Treatise on Typhoid Fever," there are three entries about heat entering the blood chamber: "If a woman contracts wind-cold, has fever and aversion to cold, and menstruation has just begun, and after seven or eight days, the fever subsides and the pulse is slow, the body is cool, and the area below the costal region is full, resembling chest binding, and she speaks incoherently, this is heat entering the blood chamber." It also says, "If a woman contracts wind-cold for seven or eight days, and continues to have alternating fever and chills at times, and menstruation is intermittent, this is heat entering the blood chamber, and the blood will definitely congeal, causing symptoms like masses, with intermittent attacks." It also says, "If a woman has typhoid fever with fever, and menstruation has just begun, she is clear-headed during the day, but speaks incoherently in the evening, as if seeing ghosts, this is heat entering the blood chamber. Do not disturb the stomach qi or the upper two jiaos, and she will heal on her own." To discuss this condition, we must first determine what the blood chamber actually is. Cheng Liaoshe's "Enlightenment on Medical Principles" believes that the blood chamber is the Chong meridian. Fang Yu and others follow this view. Ke Yunbo believes it is the liver, and Xu Lingtai believes it is both the heart and liver, all based on speculation without clear evidence. Chen Zhiming's "Effective Prescriptions for Women" believes it is the gateway to the womb, Luo Qianfu's "Hygienic Treasure Mirror" considers it the female uterus, Cheng Shishi's "Medical Essences" believes it is the uterus, and Zhang Jingyue's "Differentiation of the Triple Burner and Gate of Life" also believes it is the gateway to the womb. The "Synopsis of the Golden Chamber," in the twenty-second section on miscellaneous diseases of women, says, "If a woman has a full lower abdomen, like a mound, with slight difficulty in urination but no thirst, and this occurs after childbirth, it is because water and blood are both congealed in the blood chamber. Da Huang Gan Sui Tang is the main prescription." Therefore, what the "Treatise on Typhoid Fever" calls "fullness below the costal region, resembling chest binding" is actually in the lower abdomen. The lower abdomen is the location of the bladder and uterus. Diseases of the uterus often affect the bladder, hence the saying "slight difficulty in urination." Based on this, the views of Chen, Luo, Cheng, and Zhang are more credible. Moreover, it is only seen in women, and only during menstruation and after childbirth, which further confirms that it is the uterus. From this perspective, what is called heat entering the blood chamber is pelvic peritonitis or perimetritis. In severe cases, it can also cause meningitis, hence the incoherent speech. Women with neurasthenia often experience worsening nervous symptoms during menstruation, hence the seeing of ghosts. Mild cases can heal on their own, hence the saying "Do not disturb the stomach qi or the upper two jiaos, and she will heal on their own." Attacks occurring at regular intervals, resembling malaria, indicate pyogenic fever. I once treated a woman named Zuo whose menstruation stopped, and she had fever and severe pain and distention in the lower abdomen that was sensitive to touch. She was sent to Tongde Hospital. At that time, the director of the hospital was Dr. Pang Jingzhou. Because she was a virgin, he did not want to immediately examine her reproductive organs. Instead, he applied a plaster to her lower abdomen to observe her progress. On the third day of her admission, a large amount of white pus suddenly discharged from her vagina. From then on, her symptoms significantly decreased, and she recovered and was discharged from the hospital in a few days. This was a localized pelvic abscess (perhaps a localized appendiceal abscess) that ruptured and drained through the vagina. This is also an example of heat entering the blood chamber. However, the disease is not located within the uterus, so there is no so-called blood chamber. Calling it heat entering the blood chamber is a term of ancient imagination and speculation, which should not be used today. Modern doctors, upon seeing women with fever and incoherent speech, prescribe prescriptions with the phrase "heat entering the blood chamber" without inquiring about fullness or hardness in the lower abdomen. This can be said to be extremely thoughtless. The misuse of imaginative and speculative terms leads to such abuses.

The "Treatise on Typhoid Fever" says: "If typhoid fever has irregular or intermittent pulse, and heart palpitations, Zhigancao Tang is the main prescription." It also says, "If the pulse feels slow but occasionally stops and then resumes, it is called irregular. Also, if the pulse moves and stops, and then resumes with small beats, with a return in between, it is called irregular yin. If the pulse moves and stops, and cannot return on its own, and then resumes, it is called intermittent yin. Those who have this pulse are difficult to treat." I have already discussed irregular and intermittent pulses in my book "Critique of Huang Han Medicine." Strictly speaking, irregular and intermittent pulses correspond to premature ventricular contractions (Extrasystole) and atrioventricular block in modern medicine. To understand what premature ventricular contractions and atrioventricular block are, it is essential to understand the physiology of cardiac impulse conduction. Now, please allow me to briefly explain it.

Common Sense Questions and Answers about Diseases Cheng Hanzhang

(66) Chronic and Tuberculous Peritonitis

(Question) What is chronic peritonitis?

(Answer) It is rare in ordinary circumstances, mostly developing from acute peritonitis: or caused by trauma, abdominal fluid aspiration, or intestinal ulcer, initially becoming chronic.

(Question) What is tuberculous peritonitis?

(Answer) Tuberculous peritonitis is also a type of chronic peritonitis, caused by the invasion of the peritoneum by tubercle bacilli. It is mostly secondary to tuberculosis in other parts of the body, such as pulmonary tuberculosis, tuberculous periostitis, and tuberculous pleurisy.

(Question) What are the symptoms of these two types of peritonitis?

(Answer) The symptoms of chronic simple peritonitis and tuberculous peritonitis are the same, both with insidious onset, or sudden onset.

(Question) Do patients complain of abdominal pain like those with acute peritonitis?

(Answer) Not very painful. Only mild tenderness. The abdomen is moderately distended, but not the entire abdomen. Occasionally, the abdominal wall is flat, sunken, and tense.

(Question) What does it feel like during palpation?

(Answer) During palpation, there is localized resistance or nodular protrusions; this is due to swelling of the greater omentum or mesenteric glands.

(Question) Is there exudative fluid in the peritoneal cavity?

(Answer) Yes; but not much. And the exudative fluid is often limited to one part, so it does not flow with changes in body position like ascites.

(Question) Does the patient have a fever?

(Answer) Sometimes there is a fever.

(Question) Are there any other symptoms?

(Answer) There are also symptoms such as vomiting and hiccupping.

(Question) How should simple chronic and tuberculous peritonitis be differentiated and diagnosed?

(Answer) Just examine the patient's past medical history for wasting fever. Tuberculous exudative fluid is rich in lymphocytes and hemorrhagic, and tuberculous peritonitis lacks abdominal pain.

(Question) What is the prognosis for these two types of peritonitis?

(Answer) Non-tuberculous peritonitis has a better prognosis and can sometimes be cured. Tuberculous peritonitis is mostly dangerous. But compared to tuberculosis in other parts of the body, there is a glimmer of hope.

(Question) What is the treatment for simple chronic and tuberculous peritonitis?

(Answer) First, pay attention to food hygiene and eat more nutritious foods. Second, apply warm compresses with alcohol-dampened cloths to the abdomen, or apply ichthammol ointment, wood tar olive oil, or Voltalin ointment. Or use artificial sun lamp irradiation. Third, internal medication only uses drugs that help absorption or reduce exudation, such as iodides or pine tar preparations.

(Question) Is there a need for exploratory laparotomy?

(Answer) Tuberculous peritonitis has been cured by exploratory laparotomy and drainage. Moreover, injecting sterilized air (600-1000 cubic centimeters) after draining the fluid has great effects.

Hypertension and Arteriosclerosis (Part 1) Yue Qi

—Medical Stories, No. 9—

Hypertension and arteriosclerosis are not necessarily the same thing. Both are natural consequences of aging. In cases of hypertension, there may be arteriosclerosis present - at least in the smallest vessels. But arteriosclerosis in the peripheral vessels is not necessarily accompanied by increased blood pressure. And people whose peripheral vessels - such as those in the wrists and forehead - develop arteriosclerosis can live to a ripe old age.

Hypertension itself varies in type. Volhard and Fahr wrote a famous paper classifying hypertension into two types: "benign" and "malignant". This is indeed a perceptive classification.

Of course, measuring blood pressure has only become a common diagnostic method in the medical field in the last thirty years, but discussions of blood pressure problems began two hundred years ago. In 1733, an English clergyman named Stephen Hales measured blood pressure in horses using a very simple method. He inserted a nine-foot-long glass tube into the femoral artery of the horse. He found that the blood rose to a height of eight feet and three inches within the glass tube, indicating that the pressure of the blood was sufficient to support that height. Instruments similar to this used to measure human blood pressure began to be used by several physiologists around 1850, but only in physiological laboratories. By 1905, sufficient data from human blood pressure measurements had convinced several life insurance companies that this method of blood pressure measurement was quite useful to them. Since then, the blood pressure, lifespan, and post-mortem conditions of internal organs of millions of people have been meticulously recorded, giving general practitioners a wealth of data to study blood pressure problems.

As mentioned earlier, blood pressure increases with age. Why is this? Because in youth, blood vessels are elastic, but as the body ages, the elastic tissue of the blood vessels is gradually replaced by fibrous tissue and calcium salts, so they gradually become stiff. We know that the pressure of tap water passing through a rubber hose is lower than the pressure of water passing through an iron pipe, because the elastic rubber hose helps to squeeze the water passing through it. Arteriosclerosis affects blood pressure in much the same way. This is the "mechanical" explanation for hypertension.

This "mechanical explanation" has been criticized from various quarters. At least the general medical community does not unanimously agree with it. Now, let me list their objections and their own views, and discuss whether they have sufficient grounds.

The most forceful objection to the "mechanical explanation" is based on two facts: (1) In many cases, easily observable blood vessels - such as those in the wrists and temples - do show significant hardening, but blood pressure measurements taken with a mercury sphygmomanometer do not show an increase; (2) In some cases of extreme hypertension, the same vessels do not appear noticeably thickened. However, long ago, a scholar named Janeway tried to reconcile these seemingly contradictory facts. He pointed out that while peripheral blood vessels may harden, the internal large blood vessels - such as the common carotid artery and its branches - may still retain their elasticity, and the primary cause of change lies in these large vessels.

Arteriosclerosis is a condition that affects blood vessels differently in different parts of the body, sometimes causing an increase in blood pressure, and sometimes not.

Another objection to the "mechanical explanation" is that in some extreme cases, blood pressure rises very high, but microscopic examination of the vessel walls after death shows no change. Explanations derived from physiological laboratories can be used to explain these cases. Physiology tells us that the coat of blood vessels contains muscle tissue; also, certain nerve stimuli can cause these muscles to contract, making the vessels smaller and stiffer. These motor nerve stimuli can be created by adding solutions of certain drugs or chemicals to the bloodstream. So it is possible that a certain substance remains in the blood, causing continuous vasoconstriction, without causing permanent changes visible under a microscope. In any case, the existence of these severe forms has led astute observers - namely Volhard and Fahr - to declare that hypertension can be divided into two types, and the names they gave to these two types of hypertension are "benign" and "malignant."

An Overview of New Medicine and Hygiene in Wuxi Guo Xinghu

Wuxi is a model county in China, located in the center of the Beijing-Shanghai Railway, with convenient transportation. Waterways include the Grand Canal, and land routes include the Beijing-Shanghai Railway. In recent years, three major highways, Xicheng, Xiyi, and Xihu, have been built one after another. The Xicheng Road connects Wuxi to Jiangyin, the Xiyi Road connects Wuxi to Yixing, and the Xihu Road connects Wuxi to Shanghai, passing through Changshu, Taicang, and Jiading before reaching Shanghai. The township roads within the county are also well-developed. If one travels from Xiyi Road to Yixing, one can connect with the Beijing-Hangzhou National Highway, indicating that transportation between Wuxi and Nanjing and Hangzhou is also convenient.

In Wuxi, health administration is handled by the Public Security Bureau. Health campaigns are held every year, flies are purchased, health slogans are posted, and food stores are encouraged to install gauze covers. Every summer, the county government allocates funds to set up temporary epidemic prevention hospitals and encourages people to receive free cholera vaccinations. There are also charitable individuals in various townships who set up free clinics and medicine distribution centers. The Chinese Medicine Association also operates free clinics and medicine distribution centers, with members volunteering their services. The people of Wuxi generally do not pay attention to public health. The streets are dirty, the latrines are filthy, and the river water is turbid, allowing mosquitoes, insects, and bacteria to breed. Therefore, many people suffer from cholera and malaria every summer. Although there are street cleaners and river cleaners in the city, and latrines have been improved, citizens still do not pay attention to public health.

The Wuxi prison's daily diet and living conditions were not very hygienic in the past. Since the new prison was completed, there have been gradual improvements, but the branch offices and detention centers remain as before. Since the beginning of summer, the weather has been hot, and in recent days, the temperature has consistently been around 100 degrees. The number of detainees is crowded, and they live together in one room. The air is steaming with sweat, and the heat is overwhelming, causing epidemics to spread, and many people suddenly suffer from heatstroke and become ill.

There have been hospitals in Wuxi for nearly thirty years. The first one was the Pu Ren Hospital, founded by the American Episcopal Church in February of the 34th year of the Guangxu Emperor's reign. The superintendent, an American named Li Kele, was highly trusted by the local people. The hospital was well-equipped, with internal medicine and surgery departments, 60 beds, and more than 30 staff physicians. It was the earliest, most famous, and most complete hospital in Wuxi. Apart from the provincial public maternity hospital and the People's Hospital, Wuxi lacked large-scale public hospitals to provide convenient medical care for the poor. Since the national government strictly enforced the ban on opium, Wuxi established a county drug rehabilitation center. The funding was allocated by the provincial government, and the staff was also appointed by the provincial government. The center was located in the former Qianshan Bureau, which was later converted into a labor hospital. After the labor hospital closed down, it was converted into the current county drug rehabilitation center. The facilities are decent, accommodating 120 opium addicts. The management is relatively good. The Wuxi Semi-Charitable Hospital, the Nengren Hospital, was established with funding from the Red Swastika Society. The superintendent, Dr. Wei Zhiwen, has excellent facilities, and the fees are lower than those of private hospitals. Many private hospitals have been opened in Wuxi, but the fees are very expensive.

Wuxi has a Physicians' Association and a Wuxi branch of the Chinese Western Medicine Association, with a total of about 100 Western-trained physicians. More than 70 have registered with the Ministry of Health. Over 20 had started practicing 18 years ago, meeting the requirements for registration as revised by the Ministry of Health. Due to slow communication, more than 20 missed the registration deadline, and the Wuxi Western Medicine Association is now petitioning the provincial government to issue them practicing licenses, which is said to be promising. Based on a population of 941,372, there is one Western-trained physician for every 9,413 people.

The pharmacies in Wuxi with larger capital and better equipment include Wuzhou Pharmacy, Dalu Pharmacy, Taihe Pharmacy, and Sino-French Pharmacy. However, there are no pharmacists dispensing prescriptions. Other pharmacies, such as Zhonghe Pharmacy, Sino-Foreign Pharmacy, Xingchang Pharmacy, Sino-Western Pharmacy, Zhongnan Pharmacy, British Pharmacy, Huamei Pharmacy, and Brothers Pharmacy, specialize in selling over-the-counter medicines and cosmetics, and have a small stock of raw drugs, and engage in other businesses as well.

Common Knowledge on Hygiene of the Ears, Nose, Throat and Eyes Tang Renjin

(62) The Vocal Apparatus

The so-called vocal apparatus is the larynx, which belongs to the respiratory system. The larynx has a funnel shape. It is formed by the superposition of three unpaired cartilages and three paired cartilages. The unpaired cartilages are the cricoid cartilage, thyroid cartilage, and epiglottic cartilage. The paired cartilages are the arytenoid cartilage, corniculate cartilage, and cuneiform cartilage. These cartilages are connected to each other by the laryngeal ligaments and laryngeal muscles. Their combined action enables the function of phonation. The main part of the phonation function is the vocal cords. The vocal cords are located in the center of the larynx and are a pair of elastic ligaments. The space between the two vocal cords is called the glottis. When we breathe, the glottis immediately opens, becoming triangular (see Figure A below). When we speak, the glottis immediately closes, becoming lanceolate (see Figure B below). The ability of the glottis to open and close is the result of the movement of the laryngeal muscles. Sound can be produced when the glottis closes and air is exhaled, causing the tense vocal cords to vibrate due to the impact of the airflow. The length and tension of the vocal cords are closely related to the pitch of the sound. Therefore, the voices of women and boys under the age of fifteen are generally high-pitched, thin, and soft (no wonder they are pleasing to the ear). The voices of adult men are low and rough. This is because the vocal cords of women are short, thin, and tense. The common saying among our people that the pitch and roughness of a voice can distinguish whether or not someone is a virgin is based on the physiological changes just mentioned.

In addition, it should be noted that when we speak, we do not rely solely on the larynx, which is the vocal apparatus. When air passes through the glottis, it must be accompanied by the combined movement of the pharyngeal cavity, oral cavity, soft palate, tongue, teeth, lips, mandible, and nasal cavity before speech can be formed. If any part changes or loses its function, one will immediately experience difficulty speaking, or even be unable to speak. Therefore, in cases of pharyngeal foreign bodies, tonsillitis, stomatitis, soft palate rupture, glossitis, tooth loss, lip defects (harelip), mandibular dislocation, hypertrophic rhinitis, and nasal polyps, one often feels the pain of difficulty speaking. This is a very clear fact.

If the voice suddenly becomes hoarse, it is usually a clear indication that changes have occurred in the vocal cords. There are many causes for these changes. Based on my experience, they are generally caused by laryngitis, laryngeal foreign bodies, laryngeal tuberculosis, laryngeal syphilis, laryngeal tumors, recurrent laryngeal nerve paralysis, and singer's nodules. The detailed conditions of these several conditions have mostly been published in this journal. Readers, you should be able to recall them.

(Appendix) Hygiene of the vocal apparatus. If there is hoarseness, one should strictly adhere to (1) Refrain from talking, (2) Breathe plenty of fresh air, (3) Avoid dry, cold, and unclean air. (4) It is best to have a device for dispersing water vapor in the room (to keep the air moist), (5) Smoking, alcohol, and spicy foods can irritate the laryngeal mucosa, and should be avoided, and (6) Immediately consult a specialist physician to examine the larynx. (A) Keep the glottis open during breathing (B) Keep the glottis closed during phonation.

Popular Lectures on Modern Venereology (16) Chen Shengbai (Compiled) Yin Muqiang (Corrected)

D. Treatment and Prevention

Patients with soft chancre should maintain physical rest. Prohibit long-distance walking and strenuous exercise. Avoid excitement and stimulation of sexual desire. So as not to spread the pathogenic bacteria. And accelerate the healing of ulcers. In addition to topical antiseptics, disinfectants and lotions for external use. Systemic treatments such as autologous blood serum, protein preparations, and vaccine injections can be administered according to the symptoms. Each should choose what is appropriate.

Its prevention. Is roughly similar to general methods for preventing venereal diseases.

Chapter 2 About Lymphangitis and Lymphadenitis Due to Soft Chancre

A. Lymphangitis In the course of soft chancre. Often invades the lymphatic vessels on the back of the penis. Causing lymphangitis. The lymphatic vessels become painful, cord-like swollen masses. The skin in that area is red. Gradually softens, ruptures, drains pus, and forms chancre-like ulcers.

B. Lymphadenitis Swelling of the inguinal lymph nodes (ie, buboes). It is also a common complication of soft chancre. At this time, due to the physiological cross-walking of the genital lymph. Swelling of the inguinal lymph nodes is often seen on the opposite side of the ulcer. At the beginning of the swelling. A feeling of traction is felt when moving. Then there is pain. Walking becomes difficult. And as it grows. Either like a pigeon egg. Or like a chicken egg or larger. The skin in that area gradually becomes red, swollen, and suppurates. And accompanied by a high fever and systemic symptoms.

As for prevention and treatment. Namely, conservative rest, wet compresses, application of ointments, irradiation with X-rays, injection of vaccine and protein stimulants, and incision and drainage. Or avoid the spread of the virus, or promote the absorption of pus, or increase the body's resistance, and attempt to fundamentally kill bacteria and detoxify, etc. If applied appropriately. It can often prevent the occurrence of this disease or accelerate its cure.

Section 4 Inguinal Lymphogranuloma

Regarding Inguinal Lymphogranuloma (Lymphogranuloma inguinale), although there are not many similar records in past literature. But the definite reports related to sexual intercourse. It was Frenchmen Nicolas, Favre, and Durand in January 1913. The pathogen of this disease. Has not been discovered. It is now assumed to be a filtering pathogen. Because it is transmitted through sexual intercourse. It is also called the fourth venereal disease. The spread of this disease in China. Is also frequently seen. Unfortunately, it has not been able to attract general attention.

A. Symptoms The infection of this disease. Sexual intercourse is undoubtedly the medium. Therefore, it mostly affects young men and women. And especially men. Its symptoms include:

1. Primary Rash The incubation period of this disease is still unclear. Approximately after infection. After an incubation period of one or two weeks to several months. Epidermal peeling occurs on the glans penis or inner plate of the foreskin. Forming small ulcers, small blisters or papules. Because there are no obvious subjective symptoms. The patient is exhausted and does not know to seek medical attention.

Pain-Relieving Medicine (30) Li Xing

As scientific medicine progresses daily, it certainly cannot ignore the pain of women in labor. The current methods of pain relief involve injecting small amounts of anesthetics to relieve labor pain, or taking small amounts of analgesics. However, anesthetics should not be injected within about two hours before the baby is born, to avoid suffocation of the baby after birth. When the pain is extreme before the baby is born, the woman in labor can inhale ether during each contraction, but the amount of ether should not be excessive to avoid stopping labor. If it is a difficult birth requiring surgery, local anesthesia or ether is used.

Acute Salpingitis

As male gonorrhea is spreading rapidly, women are naturally not spared. The incidence of gonorrhea in women is directly proportional to the incidence of gonorrhea in men. Gonorrhea in women is exactly the same as in men, caused by the same diplococcus. Therefore, men can infect women, and women can also infect men, in a continuous cycle. When a woman contracts gonorrhea, the initial inflammation is in the vaginal area, and the inflammation gradually reaches the cervix internally. Sometimes, if circumstances are favorable or treatment is appropriate, the problem can be completely cured at this point. However, some people are not so lucky, and the disease reaches the cervix and then ascends through the uterine cavity to both fallopian tubes (the fallopian tubes are located in the lower abdomen, extending from the upper corners of the uterus to both sides, each about three inches long). Once gonorrhea reaches the fallopian tubes, it becomes an internal disease, and ordinary douches and internal medications cannot reach it.

Healthy fallopian tubes are slightly smaller than a pencil, but when inflamed, they swell, often reaching a diameter of more than an inch. A large amount of pus is produced inside the tubes, and the walls also thicken, becoming red and swollen. Due to these changes, the first sensation experienced by the patient is severe pain. The pain is in the lower abdomen, that is, in the pelvis, with pain on both sides of the lower abdomen. At the same time, the body also experiences chills and fever, and the discharge from the lower part also increases. The patient's appetite also decreases, and if the body is normally not obese, it inevitably becomes thin, and even if the body is obese, it will become weak. After several weeks, the condition may improve or gradually heal completely. However, if there is another infection, the problem can recur in the same way. If it occurs and subsides intermittently, it eventually becomes chronic salpingitis.

The treatment for this problem is the same as the principle for treating other types of acute inflammation. The first urgent task is to rest in bed quietly. Rest is the basic treatment for any acute inflammatory disease, and it is also an essential element of pain relief. If the painful area is moved around and not allowed to rest, it will naturally be more painful. If there is rest, the pain can be reduced, and the inflammation can gradually stop. The second method is to use heat therapy for pain relief, such as applying warm, moist heat to the lower abdomen multiple times a day. Recently, the use of artificial fever therapy has shown surprising results. The method involves using a heating device or hot water bath to raise the patient's body temperature to 105 degrees (normal body temperature is 98.6 degrees) for about four or five hours each time. This is because experiments show that gonococci cannot resist temperatures above 104 degrees for long. If the gonococci are killed by one or more artificial fever treatments, the disease will heal completely. One or more artificial fever treatments can indeed cure acute salpingitis. This method has the same effect when used for male gonorrhea. This method must be performed by an experienced physician.

Another method is to inject reaction-inducing proteins, such as sterilized defatted milk, gonococcal or other bacterial vaccines, to cause a reaction in the body and increase the body's resistance to gonococci.

Surgical Pain

People have been performing surgical procedures since the Middle Ages, but from the Middle Ages to the beginning of the 19th century, surgery did not make much progress. The reason for its lack of development was the lack of understanding of bacteriology. Performing surgical procedures without knowledge of germ theory was a dangerous and speculative undertaking. It was not until the middle of the 19th century that Joseph Lister, the patriarch of British surgery, advocated sterile surgical procedures. With an understanding of the causal relationship between bacteria and disease and methods for eliminating bacteria, surgery has made rapid progress.

The progress of surgery has opened a new chapter in scientific medicine. Some diseases that were previously fatal now have a solution, and some diseases that were previously incurable are now treatable. The contribution of surgery to mankind is truly significant.

The first factor contributing to the development of surgery was bacteriology, and the second factor was pain-relieving drugs, such as ether, local anesthetics, general anesthetics, nerve sedatives, etc. These drugs can calm or numb the patient's nerves before surgery, preventing fear and anxiety. During surgery, various anesthetics or local anesthetics can be used to make the patient unaware of the pain. After surgery, appropriate use of anesthetics can keep the patient in a state of unconsciousness and unaware of pain. The medical community worldwide continues to research new methods to reduce human suffering.

Surgery has also been introduced to our country in recent decades. The Chinese people were initially very afraid of pain, and when they had surgical diseases, they often said "afraid of pain, afraid of pain" to avoid surgery. This is human nature, and no one can be blamed. Even a surgical expert who performs surgery on others year-round will try to avoid surgery if he has a problem himself and there is a way to avoid it. Even a dental expert who extracts other people's teeth year-round will probably avoid extracting his own teeth if he has a tooth problem and there is a way to avoid it. If a surgeon treats a patient's disease as if it were his own disease when the patient cannot avoid surgery, performs appropriate surgery, and is willing to perform it on himself as he would on the patient, the patient should follow the guidance of this type of surgeon. This is the ideal surgeon and is what any country needs. To know whether surgery can be avoided, it is necessary to understand the pathology accurately. Only with a clear understanding of the pathology can it be known whether avoiding surgery is beneficial. If it is known that avoiding surgery poses a great danger, it must not be avoided, and fear of surgical pain must not be avoided. It must be known that foolish avoidance of surgery can lead to greater suffering in mild cases and danger to life in severe cases. For example, if a tumor grows on the body when it is the size of a broad bean, and one is afraid of pain and does not have it removed, waiting until the tumor grows to ten or twenty pounds before it must be removed, the pain will naturally be increased a thousandfold. As another example, if a gastric ulcer perforates, and the patient foolishly avoids surgery, the patient will have no hope of survival. Therefore, when encountering a surgical condition, both the doctor and the patient should make careful considerations in advance and then implement appropriate treatment methods. This will not only reduce pain but also preserve the safety of life.

Now, each village is sounding gongs day and night, gathering the people to rush to block it. (A special dispatch on the first)

Former Director of the Upper Yellow River Bureau – Presents Proposals for Blocking the Breach

(Jinan) Ten days ago, the breached Yellow River water diverted nine-tenths of the main flow. The depth of the Kangcun dangerous work on the north bank of the upper reaches was at most 2 zhang and 1 chi, but is now 2 zhang and 4 chi, which sufficiently indicates that the river water is gradually returning to the main river and may not change course. Wang Luhong, the former director of the Upper Yellow River Bureau, presented proposals for blocking the breach, using both old and new methods: 1. Dig a diversion river. 2. Build a diversion dam at the bend of the water flow at the head of the diversion river. Use a 30-horsepower pile driver and a 2,000-pound hammer to drive wooden piles into the river, five piles per row, spaced 10 feet apart, for a total of 85 rows. After driving all the piles, erect wooden boards on top, shaped like a floating bridge, and lay iron rails on it. Use human-powered light rail cars to dump stones. When the stones are dumped into the water, use the old-fashioned method of making a "sweep." Once the sweep box is completed, the water flow will be cut off. 3. Build five embankments and repair the water-submersible dam road. The total cost will not exceed 700,000 yuan, and the breach can be closed. (A special dispatch on the first)

Japanese Staff Officer Tangxie Comforts Disaster Victims in Western Shandong

(Jinan) Today, Tangxie, a staff officer of the Japanese army stationed in Tianjin, and Ishino, a Japanese military officer stationed in Jinan, traveled to western Shandong by plane to comfort disaster victims. The provincial government sent personnel to receive them. Reporters went along and saw that within the 5,000-square-mile disaster area, it was like a vast ocean, with villages and county towns like islands. Fields of crops were still submerged in water, and there was no sign of people, which was extremely tragic. Jiaxiang, Jining, and Wen were especially severe. They returned to Jinan in the afternoon, and Ishino and others flew back to Tianjin by the original plane. (A special dispatch on the first)

North China Economic Commission – Finds a Suitable Address in Tianjin – East Asia Economic Association to be Established Tomorrow

(Tianjin) The North China Economic Relief Commission, initiated by Gao Lingshou, Wang Shuangqi, and others, has found a suitable address on Penglai Street in the Japanese Concession and will start operations immediately. Its capital is entirely borne by the Tianjin branch of the Tokyo International Bank. The East Asia Economic Association is scheduled to be established on the 3rd, with Niu Chuanshan, Shen Tongwu, Liu Xiangye, and others in charge. This company's nature differs slightly from that of the North China Economic Relief Commission, but its purpose is the same, under the command of Takagi Chenlang of the Sino-Japanese Industrial Company and the Kwantung Army of the South Manchuria Railway. It specializes in survey and introduction work to provide targets for foreign investment. Japanese industrialists Miyagi Ryōzō, Akashi Tomosuke, and Irikawadai Saburō arrived in Tianjin from Shanhaiguan on the 1st to investigate the paper-making and other industries in Beiping, Tianjin, Hebei, and Chahar. (A special dispatch on the first)

(Tianjin) The Tianjin Chamber of Commerce held a joint meeting of executive and supervisory committees on the first, deciding to immediately organize the East Asia Tonghui Trading Company and electing Pan Yansheng, Bian Shoujing, Yu Fuchun, and nine others as preparatory committee members, with Pan Yansheng designated as the director of the preparatory committee. The association's purpose is to advocate international economic cooperation. (A special dispatch on the first)

Central Government Approves Funds for Hubei

(Hankou) The central government approved Zhang Qun's request and agreed to allocate 3 million yuan to implement work relief and repair civilian dikes. Chiang telegraphed the provincial government, ordering the rapid repair of the Shi-Rong Highway to facilitate traffic between Sichuan and Hubei. (A special dispatch on the first)

(Nanjing) Zhang Qun, Chairman of Hubei, returned to Nanjing on the morning of the first. According to him, he discussed methods of relieving the Hubei disaster with various parties in Shanghai and has considerable hope. He has a plan to relieve disaster victims in Hubei and discussed it with Minister Kong in Shanghai, who was extremely concerned and expressed support for the plan, but the specific details have not yet been finalized. He has now come to Nanjing to continue discussing with relevant central government agencies, hoping to make a decision soon. He has been away from his post for a long time and will return to Hubei in two or three days. (A special dispatch on the first)

Liao Zhongkai's Burial Ceremony Held Yesterday at Tianbao City, Zijin Mountain

(Nanjing) Liao Zhongkai's coffin was interred at the Tianbao City cemetery on the morning of the first. More than 40 representatives from central committees, party, government, and military agencies, as well as military academy students, all went to perform the rituals. (A special dispatch on the first)

(Nanjing) The burial ceremony of revolutionary martyr Liao Zhongkai was held at 10 a.m. on the 1st at the Tianbao City cemetery on Zijin Mountain. Before 9 a.m., a ceremony was first held at the Zhigong Hall of Linggu Temple, where the coffin had been placed. Those present included central committee members Ye Chucang, He Yingqin, Dai Chuanxian, Shao Yuanchong, Shi Ying, Zhu Peide, Zhang Qun, Ma Chaojun, Zhu Jiahua, Zhou Qigang, Chen Gongbo, Zhang Zhen, Chu Minyi, Hong Ludong, Chen Shuren, Jiao Yitang, Miao Peicheng, Xiao Jishan, Duan Xipeng, Zheng Zhannan, Wang Qi, Pan Yunchao, Deng Feihuang, Ji Liang, Zhang Zhizhong, Education Director of the Military Academy, Gui Yongqing, Li Minghao, the entire delegation of officers and students of the Military Academy, Xiao Tongzi, Di Ying, Yang Donglin, secretaries of various departments of the Central Party Headquarters, and staff members, as well as representatives from various agencies and people's organizations Chen Daqi, Xu Chonghao, and others, totaling about several thousand people. Madam He Xiangning, Liao Zhongkai's widow, led the Liao family to preside over the ceremony and reciprocated the greetings. President Wang had originally planned to return from Shanghai to participate, but because he still needed a follow-up examination in Shanghai, he was unable to return to Nanjing to participate. He sent a telegram to Chen Shuren to express his apologies to Madam Liao on his behalf. Ma Xiang, the director of the Mausoleum Guard Office, personally led the police to maintain order. At 9 o'clock sharp, music was played to raise the coffin, which was immediately moved into the hearse and driven along the road outside the mausoleum towards the Tianbao City cemetery. The delegation of officers and students of the Military Academy lined up to lead the way. Participants and Madam Liao, among others, also rode in cars to escort the hearse. The line of vehicles stretched for several miles, which was quite spectacular. At 10 a.m., the hearse arrived at the cemetery. After the coffin was moved into the burial pit, the burial ceremony was held. Ye Chucang, a member of the Central Standing Committee, presided over the ceremony, offering a wreath from the Central Executive and Supervisory Committees, and leading everyone in paying the highest respects to Liao Zhongkai's spirit. After the dirge was played, the ceremony concluded and everyone dispersed. According to Chen Shuren, the director of the burial preparation committee, the preliminary design of Liao's tomb has now been drafted and approved by Madam Liao. The construction of the tomb will be simple and unadorned, with only a large monument erected in front of the tomb and a plaza opened up to allow people to pay their respects. Bids will be solicited immediately for construction. Once the project is completed, a public memorial ceremony will be held at a later date. (A Central News Agency dispatch on the first)

(Nanjing) Zhang Qun arrived in Nanjing by train from Shanghai on the morning of the 1st, immediately participating in Liao Zhongkai's burial ceremony and visiting He Yingqin and others. It is said that he will return to Hubei within days. (A Central News Agency dispatch on the first)

Feng Yuxiang Plans to Have Important Proposals for the Sixth Plenary Session

(Nanjing) Feng Yuxiang plans to have important proposals for the Sixth Plenary Session, which will be entrusted to Central Committee member Li Liejun to bring to Nanjing. (A special dispatch on the first)
